  3: "It still doesn\'t feel real. Years of scrimping and saving, and I finally have the cozy little cabin in the middle of the woods that I\'ve always dreamed of. No landlords, no trains howling past my room at night, and no damned NEIGHBORS."
  3: "Unfortunately... I\'ve also discovered why the last owner was willing to sell the place for so cheap. It\'s a total wreck. The floor\'s rotting, the roof leaks, the windows rattle. Earlier, I found a damn raccoon living in the pantry!"
  3: "Also, I\'m fairly certain the place is haunted. I keep hearing odd whispers, or spotting shadows in my peripheral vision. Doors will fly open without warning, without any wind."
  3: "And... there are moments when I\'ll enter a dark room, just before I turn on the lights, when I swear I\'m not alone. I have this inescapable sensation that I\'ve entered into a space that belongs to someone else... Or <i>something</i> else."
  3: "Oh well. I\'ve had roommates before. Whatever lives here, we\'ll just have to learn to get along."
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "I\'m starting to think it\'s not the house that\'s haunted. It\'s the river. Maybe the whole damn forest."
  3: "After months of swearing, sweating, and stubbed toes, I\'m all but done with the repairs to the house. Today\'s task was patching the holes in the roof. Turned out there were a few more than I thought, and in a fit of stubbornness I stayed out working a little later than I should have."
  3: "As it started getting dark, I kept thinking I could hear someone whispering. But every time I stopped pounding nails long enough to listen, the whispers would suddenly stop."
  3: "I thought I was hearing things at first, but it got worse the darker it got. By the time the stars came out, I was surrounded."
  3: "Voices, shadows, strange lights... a presence. Not a ghost, but something bigger. Something older. A kind of Power that thrummed in the air all around me."
  3: "I should have been terrified, but for some reason, I wasn\'t. It didn\'t feel malicious at all. Mostly it seemed curious. Even... playful?"
  3: "This place is strange. But there\'s a beauty here, too. And now that I have the house fixed up, I finally have the time to get to know it."
  3: "In more mundane news, some development company has started sending me letters, asking if I would consider selling my land. (Can you believe that? Just as I\'ve gotten the damn place fixed up.)"
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "That development group that\'s after the property has found a cunning new tactic: this morning they sent a handsome man in a little bowtie to knock on my door. I knew he was here to convince me to sell, but he had a nice smile, and he was quick with the witty chit-chat, so I invited him to share a walk with me."
  3: "We took a stroll down by the river, and almost had a nice time. Unfortunately, since I have no intention of selling my land, our conversation quickly turned into an argument. I told him to get off my property and stormed away."
  3: "Then I heard a splash."
  3: "I turned around just in time to see him vanish under the water. I thought he must have tripped at first, but I\'ve been replaying the moment in my head, and the more I do, the more convinced I am that what actually happened is, the river rose up and grabbed him."
  3: "I leapt in after him, but by the time I got the poor fool to shore, he was half-drowned and completely terrified. Without another word, he ran to his car and drove off."
  3: "I don\'t know why, but I\'m positive that what happened was my doing. The Power in this place... it was responding to <i>my</i> anger. I\'m connected to it, somehow."
  3: "I have to learn more..."
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "Ever since that incident with the man from the development group, I\'ve been searching for answers... following some sixth sense I don\'t understand on longer and longer journeys into the woods."
  3: "Yesterday, it led to me to the ruins of an old house, near Westchester."
  3: "From the moment I arrived, the place felt... wrong. Sick, somehow. The light didn\'t behave the way light is supposed to. There were whispers in the air, but they sounded so much darker than the ones around my home. The place reminded me of a crypt. Against every instinct, I crept closer, and peered in through a window."
  3: "It was dark inside, and hazy. There were cobwebs everywhere, and roots growing up through the walls. But I could make out a shape. Something standing in the corner. It looked almost like a person..."
  3: "And then it turned around. And it was NOT a person."
  3: "I\'ve never run so hard in my life."
  3: "Everything gets hazy after that. I remember tripping over something. Falling. I think I must have hit my head?"
  3: "When I woke up, I was in the home of a strange old woman (with an even stranger pet). She introduced herself as Cora, and told me that she was the \'Keeper\' of these woods. And she\'d been expecting me."
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "It\'s a Sunday evening. Chilly. I\'m sitting on the deck, watching the sunset through the trees, thinking about everything I now know. And what comes next."
  3: "Cora says there\'s a Power that flows through these woods, pooling in places like the ruins near Westchester, and the river near my home. She says it calls out those who can hear it. Those like her... and me."
  3: "But there\'s even more she doesn\'t say, because she doesn\'t need to. I can feel it, this Power. It\'s bigger than all of us... a swift-moving river so wide you can\'t see the shore and so deep you can\'t touch the bottom."
  3: "It\'s not good or evil, but it is volatile. It responds to intention. Cora says that those who respect it, who nurture and protect it, can use it to do good things."
  3: "But what about those who don\'t?"
  3: "\'He used to be a person.\' That\'s what Cora said, when I asked her about the creature in the ruins. Redfield. She told me about him... about the choices he made, and how they corrupted him. How that corruption has rippled down over the years. So many lives broken. So many innocent people hurt."
  3: "Was it malice that drove him? Or just arrogant, selfish ignorance?"
  3: "I guess there\'s no difference in the end..."
  3: "I told Cora about the development group sniffing around my land, and the two of us are agreed: they absolutely cannot be allowed to build here."
  3: "This river must be protected. So I will be the one to protect it."
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "That man from the development group is back. Under different circumstances, I might be happy about that."
  3: "Unfortunately, he brought friends. I\'ve been seeing trucks in the woods for weeks. I keep sneaking out to slash their tires, but no matter how many I slash, there are always more the next day. They\'re persistent, I\'ll give them that. They\'re buying up all the land around here. And they still want mine."
  3: "Which means that every day, I see his car come down the drive. Every day, I hear his footsteps on the porch, his knock on the door, three times, tap-tap-tap. Every day I see his smiling face through the screen, straightening his little bowtie and taking off his little hat."
  3: "And every day he asks, \'Will you reconsider selling?\'"
  3: "And every day I answer, \'Not for sale.\'"
  3: "Until today. Today something different happened. Today I opened the door, and the question he asked me was, \'Would you have dinner with me sometime?\' I was shocked he had the nerve... and even more shocked that I said yes!"
  3: "What the hell is wrong with me?"
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "I\'ve been pacing all day. Everything is happening so fast. I can\'t stop thinking about that night at the waterfall... his kiss on my neck. I keep telling myself it\'s just infatuation between us, just a stupid, amazing crush, but..."
  3: "Damn it, I\'m falling for him. There, it\'s down on paper now. The awful truth."
  3: "But I <i>can\'t</i> fall for him! He works for the development group that wants to rip this forest apart, and I can\'t let that happen. The river that runs through my land, and the Power within it, have to be protected from these people."
  3: "But they also need protected from it. The Power won\'t just let them do as they please. I can already feel it starting to get restless. Agitated. Hell, it almost killed a man just for raising his voice at me. How will it react when they finally start up those bulldozers, and start cutting down trees? Building their town? Raising a dam?"
  3: "Where does it stop? How does it end? Who gets hurt, before this is over?"
  3: "I keep circling back to a very dumb idea: What if I just told him the truth? Cora made me promise I wouldn\'t tell anyone about the Power, but... could I make him understand? Could he make THEM understand?"
  3: "And if so... what happens then?"
  3: ""
  3: "Dear Journal,"
  3: "Arthur stayed over a few nights ago, and despite myself... I told him everything. I didn\'t mean to. It just happened. One minute we were talking about taking a camping trip, and the next I was blurting out everything I know about the river and the Power within it."
  3: "He thought I was pulling his leg at first, so I took him to the ruins near Westchester. I made him walk up and look in the window."
  3: "Needless to say, he believed me after that. In fact, he was so worked up he wanted to call the paper! But I told him what could happen if word got out about this place. I made him promise to keep it a secret. And he agreed."
  3: "The next day he confronted the development group. I can only imagine what dramatic speech he made them, but whatever he said got through. They\'re pulling back the trucks, slowing down construction, and redrawing their plans to better protect the river."
  3: "And I\'ve got plans of my own: a rite Cora showed me, for bonding with the Power in order to better protect it. But I\'m adding a new element with a marlinspike: a safeguard to ensure that I won\'t ever become like that thing in the ruins... or hurt the ones I love."

  3: "But we both know there\'s no risk of that, is there?"
